        <p class="date">
         Wed Aug 08, 2012 at 08:00 AM PDT
        </p>
        <h2>
         <a href="/story/2012/08/08/1102903/-Homemade-bird-bath" id="titleHref">
          Homemade bird bath.
         </a>
         <span style="white-space: nowrap">
         </span>
        </h2>
        <p class="author">
         <span>
          by
         </span>
         <a href="/user/burnt out">
          burnt out
         </a>
         <a alt="Follow this author" class="ajax type-user do-hotlist do-updateContent size-tiny off altTooltip" href="#?friend_id=278494&amp;is_stream=1">
          Follow
         </a>
         <span class="for">
          for
         </span>
         <a href="/blog/Backyard Science">
          Backyard Science
         </a>
        </p>
        <ul class="front-page-share clearfix">
         <li style="margin-left: 0px">
          <div class="fb-share-button" data-href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/08/08/1102903/-Homemade-bird-bath" data-layout="button_count">
          </div>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="twitter-share-button" data-count="horizontal" data-related="markos" data-text="Homemade bird bath." data-url="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/08/08/1102903/-Homemade-bird-bath" data-via="dailykos" href="https://twitter.com/share">
           Tweet
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a class="comments comment_count_with_new" data-comment_count="133" data-story_id="1102903" href="/story/2012/08/08/1102903/-Homemade-bird-bath#comments">
           133 Comments
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>
       <div class="article-body">
        <div id="intro">
         <p>
          A few days ago I made a
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/comments/1116622/47031210">
           comment
          </a>
          in a
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/story/2012/08/04/1116622/-More-Extreme-Heat-Drought-and-Fires">
           diary
          </a>
          by Green Mother in which I told about a bird bath I had made that consisted of a reservoir and pump that recirculated the water thus keeping it a bit cooler than the water in my other bird baths. In this terrible heat that so many of us are experiencing this year a lot of people, including myself, are having trouble with the water in our bird baths heating up to the point that it's too hot for the birds to drink and/or evaporating faster than we can fill them. With a lot of the normal water holes dried up this summer, a place for the birds to get a cool drink is more important than ever. Several people showed an interest in it and asked how I had built it. I promised to do a short diary on it and will attempt to do so here.
         </p>
        </div>
        <p class="divider-doodle">
        </p>
        <div class="article-body" id="body">
         <p>
          .
          <br/>
          I started this diary trying to explain every step in detail but when I went back and re-read what I had written it sounded confusing so I decided to hit the delete button and start over. I'm just not very good at explaining things so I think I'll just go with the
          <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KISS_principle">
           KISS
          </a>
          principle in way of explanation. That's also the method I went with when building this bird bath. I'll just post some pics accompanied by a brief description and see how that works. If you have any questions please ask and I'll answer them the best I can.
         </p>
         <p>
          I guess the first pic should be the finished product and then I'll go back and outline the process to get there. This is what it looks like when all put together. I still have a few things to finish up yet but with the extreme heat that we've had this year I got in a hurry to put it into service so pushed things a bit and will go back and tie up the loose ends later.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn2861.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn2861.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          Under that stack of rocks is this 15 gallon plastic drum that I got free from a local business that was glad to get rid of it once they had used up the ingredients. Ask around and chances are you can find a free one too. You could even do this with a five gallon bucket if that's all you could find. All I had to do was to cut the top off with a reciprocating saw and give it a good cleaning.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=rockhunt002-1.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/rockhunt002-1.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I went out this morning and took the top center pieces off to give you a view of the bowl and to show you how it was put together. The four inch PVC pipe in the center serves three purposes. It allows me access to the pump without taking the whole bowl off. I've had to pull the pump twice to clean the filter since I first put it in service a couple months ago. Sunflower seeds and such are what I found clogging it both times. I intend to put some screen wire over the drain holes and that should solve that problem.
         </p>
         <p>
          I also fill the drum with water through this pipe. It saves me taking the whole bowl off just to add water. I've had to refill it twice but the first time was because I had the water level set a bit too high and it was dribbling over the back edge and I didn't realize it for awhile. I filled it for the third time this morning since I already had the center piece off but it was still almost half full and could have went another couple weeks or more.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn2843.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn2843.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I said the PVC pipe served three purposes . The third thing it does is to give the water a way to get recirculated back to the drum. The holes you see are drilled at whatever height you want your water level to be. You can see that I have a lot of holes, of varying sizes and varying heights. That's just due to poor engineering on my part. That's what I get for being in a hurry.... The first set I drilled were too high and the water overflowed and ran over the edge of the bowl. Then I drilled some more at a lower position but they were too small and didn't keep up with the pump and it still overflowed. So I got a bigger drill bit and put in a couple more holes and now finally have it about right. You'll just have to experiment with it a bit until you have the right amount of holes for your pump. Go slow, it's easier to drill them than to plug them if you get too many. I'm sure that an engineer could come up with a formula using the pump volume output numbers to find the exact size and number of holes to drill but my way works too.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn2840.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn2840.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I placed a terracotta planter over the pipe, both to hide the pipe and also as a raised platform for the saucer to sit on. You could use all kinds of things for this but most people probably already have a couple of these clay pots laying around. The height isn't critical, whatever you have on hand or whatever you like will be fine. A couple of old red bricks would work as well.
         </p>
         <p>
          I placed a few small flat rocks under the planter too raise it up off the bottom of the bowl to allow water to pass under it. I plan to make something a bit more stable for it to stand on but haven't got around to it yet. Actually I have a few things to do before it is completely finished. The screen filter that I mentioned for one and the rocks that are just stacked rather precariously need to be mortared in place, and right now I am just using an extension cord run from the house to power the pump and I intend to bury an electric cable if the ground ever gets soft enough that I can dig without using a pick.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn2845.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn2845.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          On top of the planter I put a terracotta saucer. I could not find one with a center hole so I had to drill one. It can be done but slow and easy is the word. Terracotta pots, as everyone probably already knows, are brittle and crack easily. Use a sharp masonry bit and don't push too hard while drilling.
         </p>
         <p>
          I originally put it right side up but found that when the water filled up and ran over the edge that instead of dripping off, it clung to the saucer and followed it all the way back to the pipe where it then ran down the side of the pipe and back into the bowl. I expect if my pump had a bigger discharge volume that wouldn't be a problem. But actually it wasn't really a problem as far as the work ability of the system except that there was no sound of the water dripping and I believe that that watery sound helps to draw the birds to it. So anyways, I turned it upside down and lo and behold it worked that way. Strange, but true. I'm not satisfied with that though because I'd like to have the top serve as another drinking/bathing area for the birds. Working on solving that problem but haven't come up with a solution yet, but I will. I'll probably end up making a new bowl with a bit different design. Meanwhile the upside down saucer will have to do. You may have noticed in one of the pics above that there is a different bowl for the center piece. It was one that I originally made for that purpose but the water clung to it just like it did the saucer. I tried inverting that also but it didn't work with that one. Puzzling....
          <br/>
          Here is a pic of all the top center pieces.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn3160.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn3160.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          This is just a hollow rock that I robbed from one of our rock gardens. I put it on top of everything to hide the end of the hose. Not necessary, just thought it looked better.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=Dscn2850.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/Dscn2850.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I made the bowl out of concrete. It is a bit tricky but if I can do it, so can you. I used an old saucer sled for a form to help me shape it. I had one that's hung in the barn for several years but if you don't happen to have one, they are cheap, though they might be hard to find this time of year, especially if you happen to live in an area that gets no snow..... But look around and see what you can come up with. Old unwanted satellite dishes are everywhere these days. The lid of a large trash can would work too. If nothing else you could just mound up some dirt, with your short length of pipe in the center, shape it into an inverted bowl and pack it down real good and pour your cement right on top of it.
         </p>
         <p>
          The tricky part is getting the mix the right consistency. Too dry and the concrete will be weak and crumbly, too wet and it will sag downwards before it drys. Mine was just a bit too dry and because of that it's got a lot of tiny voids and looks a little rough but it seems to be strong enough, at least I haven't broken it yet. Follow the mixing directions on the bag and go easy on the water additions. Add a bit of water, mix, add a bit more, mix some more, etc. etc. until you can work it and yet it doesn't slump .
         </p>
         <p>
          Here is a pic of the saucer sled with a hole cut in the center with the short end of pipe stuck through the hole. I simply laid this on a flat surface and covered it with concrete. The saucer sled forms the inside of the bowl and you just free form the outside using a small hand trowel and your own hands. Try to keep the thickness as uniform as possible, though it's not critical as long as you don't end up with it being so thin in parts as to weaken it. Wear some rubberized or latex gloves.
         </p>
         <p>
          It's not hard to do this if you have the concrete the right consistency, impossible if you don't. If you get the mix too wet you can add some more cement to dry it up a bit. I laid a piece of burlap over the sled before putting the concrete on. I did that thinking that the imprint of it would leave a rough surface that would make it less slippery for the birds but that turned out to be unnecessary and won't do that on the next one.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=wednesday039.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/wednesday039.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          This is what I used. It's available at any hardware store. Or you can buy straight cement and add sand to it. About six parts sand to one part cement should do it.You can probably get a smoother finish going that route if you'd prefer that.The dye isn't necessary, in fact now that it's done I think I prefer the natural grey concrete color, but you can use it or not as you wish. I think there are a few other colors available too.
          <br/>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=wednesday042.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/wednesday042.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          That's all there is to it. Basically it's a barrel with a bowl on top and a pump inside that pumps water up to the bowl where it drains back when it reaches the desired depth, Don't hesitate to ask if you have any questions. I know my explanation probably leaves a lot to be desired.
         </p>
         <p>
          If I had it to do over again I would use a six inch pipe as it's a tight fit getting my pump up through the four inch hole. It just barely fits. And a bigger pump would probably be better too. I used what I had on hand.
         </p>
         <p>
          It's not artwork and it's not going to win any beauty awards and may not be something you want cluttering up your back yard. I don't like the look of manicured lawns myself so it fits right in with my scruffy one, and it does what I wanted it to do, brings in the birds and gives em a cool drink.
         </p>
         <p>
          Hope I haven't made it look more complicated than it is, because it really isn't. I'll try to answer any and all questions. I'll close this diary with a few pics of the birds that use it.
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=threebirdsatbath.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/threebirdsatbath.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=summertanagermalegettingadrink.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/summertanagermalegettingadrink.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=redwingatbath2.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/redwingatbath2.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=indigobuntingdrinking2.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/indigobuntingdrinking2.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=chickadeeatbath.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/chickadeeatbath.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=bluebirdandgoldfinchatnewbath.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/bluebirdandgoldfinchatnewbath.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=cardinalatbath.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/cardinalatbath.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=goldfinchmaledrinking.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/goldfinchmaledrinking.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          <a href="http://s1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/?action=view%C2%A4t=tufftytakingabath.jpg" target="_blank">
           <img alt="Photobucket" border="0" src="http://i1172.photobucket.com/albums/r569/flyingcarp/tufftytakingabath.jpg"/>
          </a>
         </p>
         <p>
          I want to add that it was a
          <a href="http://www.dailykos.com/comments/1084031/45766861">
           comment and pics
          </a>
          by enhydra lutris back in April of a fountain birdbath overflowing with cedar waxwings that inspired me to build this in the first place. Haven't got a flock like that in mine yet but there's always tomorrow. So thanks for the inspiration enhydra!
         </p>
         <p>
          One final note; if you decide to build one and you have a problem or a question pops up in the middle of the job, message me here and I'll get back to you as soon as I see it.
         </p>
         <p>
          <span class="update">
           <a href="/story/2012/08/08/1102903/-Homemade-bird-bath#20120809045256" name="20120809045256">
            <b>
             Thu Aug 09, 2012 at 4:52 AM PT
            </b>
           </a>
           :
          </span>
          KenBee chastised me, and rightfully so, because I had not mentioned the importance of powering the pump through a circuit containing a Ground Fault Interrupter, or
          <a href="http://www.naturalhandyman.com/iip/infelectrical/infgfi.html">
           GFI
          </a>
          as they are commonly known. For anyone who doesn't know, a GFI is basically a circuit breaker that is designed to trip instantaneously in the event of a short or ground. It's to protect you from being electrocuted.
         </p>
         <p>
          I apologize for neglecting to talk about this very important point in the diary and wish to thank Ken Bee for bringing it to my attention.
         </p>
         <br/>
        </div>
       </div>

          <p>
           <b>
            More Tagging tips:
           </b>
          </p>
          <p>
           A tag is a way to search for this diary. If someone is searching for "Barack Obama," is this a diary they'd be trying to find?
          </p>
          <p>
           Use a person's full name, without any title. Senator Obama may become President Obama, and Michelle Obama might run for office.
          </p>
          <p>
           If your diary covers an election or elected official, use election tags, which are generally the state abbreviation followed by the office. 
		CA-01 is the first district House seat. CA-Sen covers both senate races. NY-GOV covers the New York governor's race.
          </p>
          <p>
           Tags do not compound: that is, "education reform" is a completely different tag from "education". A tag like "reform" alone is probably not meaningful.
          </p>

             <div class="ct">
              <p>
               main thing is that it has to develop enough head pressure to raise the water from the bottom of the barrel to the top of it. That will be stated in feet I think. It should give you that head height on the pump package. As long as it has enough pressure to do that then you can balance things by the size and number of holes that you drilled. My pump is very small, I wish it was a little bigger so as to have a little more flow thus making a larger, and noisier, waterfall.

           <p>
            You should see my bird bath. On second thought, you shouldn't. I would be embarrassed. I set a plastic toboggan on the ground with some water and a big stick in it.
           </p>
           <p>
            You get to see so many visitors and watch them play in the water. That would be very enjoyable and calming. Plus, you get to photograph them.
           </p>

            <em>
             Such a cooling and refreshing project. Thank you, burnt out. Nicely done.

         <li id="c65">
          <div class="cx" id="cx47077249">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             I just use a plastic plant saucer
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1102903/47077249#c65?mode=alone;showrate=1#c65">
              7+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:278494">
               burnt out
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:10803">
               cotterperson
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:257122">
               belinda ridgewood
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:163899">
               Polly Syllabic
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:65625">
               Knucklehead
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:70454">
               KenBee
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:31022">
               sockpuppet
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             on the ground for the turkeys and sometimes fawns use it too.
            </p>
            <p>
             For the other birds I put a ceramic plant saucer on a small round metal table. It allows some space around the saucer for the birds to perch before they approach the saucer. For decoration - I have a cast iron bird in the middle to give them the idea.
            </p>
            <p>
             I change the water daily but all in all it couldn't be simpler.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">
            <p class="sig">
             Free at last
            </p>
            <p class="cb">
             by
             <a href="/user/uid:293782">

          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Very nice.. that large reservoir is a nice idea.. less filling it!
           </p>
           <p>
            Our current bird bath is simply one that usually holds standing water - about 4-5 inches deep. But I bought a tiny water pump and stuck it to the bottom and simply stuck 3 inches of clear tubing in the outlet. It barely sticks up above the surface and provides a nice little fountain with sufficient gurgling but not enough to scare the birds.
           </p>
           <p>
            What I find amazing, is watching the wasps come to take a drink! They land on the edge and slowly creep up to the water to take their drink.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

               <p>
                First I commend you on thinking of our diminutive neighbors &amp; photography subjects, especially in this very hot summer (in most places.)
                <br/>
                Here we have feeders, half a dozen bird baths &amp; multiple water dishes for the dogs.
                <br/>
                In an alcove at the front entry, we have a very well visited fountain.
                <br/>
                It`s not there as a fountain but as a birdbath &amp; is kept spotless at all times. (Teri does that usually)
                <br/>
                A fountain one would be less inclined to clean since a nice patina of algae is cool in my book.
               </p>
               <p>
                Here`s the one we have by the front entry to our place.
                <br/>
                There are also hummingbird feeders hanging there so they can clean up before dinner.
               </p>
               <p>
                Good evening to all who love &amp; care for the wee ones who visit us for our pleasure.

          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            what a great DYI project
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47076079#c39?mode=alone;showrate=1#c39">
             15+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:163899">
              Polly Syllabic
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:327297">
              PHScott
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:118312">
              lineatus
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:278494">
              burnt out
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:293187">
              cassandracarolina
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:302707">
              jim in IA
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:56610">
              ladybug53
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:69925">
              martyc35
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:60601">
              FindingMyVoice
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:10803">
              cotterperson
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:257122">
              belinda ridgewood
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:237560">
              Trotskyrepublican
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:34327">
              Damnit Janet
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:9653">
              Debby
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:31022">
              sockpuppet
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I've got a solar pump that sits in my larger bird bath and brings a lot more birds to the water.
           </p>
           <p>
            This summer I had to add a long rock that sits just above the waterline because the local bees were coming to drink at the bowl.
           </p>
           <p>
            It was very weird at first to see a half dozen bees gulping down the water while hanging onto the rock just above the water line. They didn't even flinch when my shadow would fall on them, they were so thirsty.
           </p>
           <p>
            We're getting some monsoon rains, which is a blessing, but it won't break the long term drought, and surface water will dry up quickly without daily recharges from the sky.
           </p>
           <p>
            thanks to everyone who spares a little food and water, a little space, for the wild, no matter where you live.
           </p>
          </div>

           <p class="sig">

             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:70454">
              KenBee
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:31022">
              sockpuppet
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I made one that was much simpler - no moving water. I keep meaning to go back and add a pump because it would attract so many more visitors, and your plan is a good nudge.
           </p>
           <p>
            Mine is just a saucer set on top of a tomato cage, with salvia planted around the base. The salvia serves two purposes - attacts/feeds hummingbirds (this was a few years ago and it has a lot more blooms now), and it creates a buffer so cats can't sneak up and ambush birds in the bath. It's open enough above that they can watch for hawks, and can drop down in to the foliage if they feel threatened. Splash water from the bath keeps the salvia watered. (And droppings keep it fertilized.)
           </p>
           <p>
            <a href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/lineatus/666452341/" title="simple birdbath by lineatus, on Flickr">
             <img alt="simple birdbath" height="413" src="http://farm2.staticflickr.com/1343/666452341_45743cf342.jpg" width="399"/>
            </a>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Aside from being perfect for your feathered friends, it is beautiful to look at, and I expect the sound of the water is also relaxing.
           </p>
           <p>
            I am forwarding a link for this diary to several family members who love watching birds.
           </p>
           <p>
            I think your photos and instructions in the text are clear and would help even a mechanically challenged person like myself to build something similar.
           </p>
           <p>
            Wonderful! and thx again!
           </p>
          </div>

          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Do you have any good tips
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47076239#c44?mode=alone;showrate=1#c44">

         <li id="c49">
          <div class="cx" id="cx47076393">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Hydrogen peroxide works great.
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1102903/47076393#c49?mode=alone;showrate=1#c49">
              21+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:9043">
               surfbird007
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:278494">
               burnt out
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:302707">
               jim in IA
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:214528">
               ParkRanger
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:163899">
               Polly Syllabic
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:3590">
               hester
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:56610">
               ladybug53
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:327297">
               PHScott
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:69925">
               martyc35
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:60601">
               FindingMyVoice
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:166753">
               Lady Libertine
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:31985">
               milton333
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:10803">
               cotterperson
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:257122">
               belinda ridgewood
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:10240">
               Sherri in TX
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:26703">
               oceanview
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:315714">
               DamselleFly
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:34327">
               Damnit Janet
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:9653">
               Debby
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:70454">
               KenBee
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:31022">
               sockpuppet
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             I buy the stuff from a local beauty supply store--17% concentration rather than the 3% you get at the drug store--by the gallon. A couple of tablespoons in an average size birdbath is all it takes. The water will stay crystal clear, and the birdbath will not grow furry stuff in it. It's harmless to the birds. You can even use it in small ponds since it is harmless to plants and fish.
            </p>
            <p>
             The birds use my birdbaths more since I started using this method. I think they prefer clean water.
            </p>

         <li id="c77">
          <div class="cx" id="cx47079662">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             Lavender in bird bath
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1102903/47079662#c77?mode=alone;showrate=1#c77">
              8+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:278494">
               burnt out
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:26703">
               oceanview
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:315714">
               DamselleFly
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:34327">
               Damnit Janet
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:9653">
               Debby
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:163899">
               Polly Syllabic
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:70454">
               KenBee
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:31022">
               sockpuppet
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             I have several different types of Lavender growing in my garden and put a sprig of Lavender in the bird bath water when I change it. The Lavender helps keep algae from growing and it's not toxic to the birds.
            </p>
           </div>

            <div class="ct">
             <p>
              if there is shelter near the small birds nee the quick shelter from Hawks, a short flight path to safety.
             </p>
             <p>
              Hawks stake out bird baths and bird feeders,,big surprise!
             </p>
             <p>
              shelter can be a shrub like Lineatus's, a dense tree someplace nearby they can suss out the scene and see if it's safe before bathing.
             </p>
             <p>
              so would you if you were 3 " long.
             </p>
             <p>
              amiright?
             </p>
             <p>
              and burnt: EXTENSION CORD?!?!?!?!
             </p>
             <p>
              seriously amigo, you need to get that right before you fry yer bad self!
             </p>
             <p>
              I hope it's on a GFI outlet but even that I hope it's temporary, I see you are on track for a solar pump. Stay safe, and a permanent extension cord across your lawn, even outdoor low voltage landscaping power is a bit of a stretch safety wise.
             </p>
             <p>
              <em>
               (Outdoors, in a garden, sink, bath, kitchen utility room all require GFI protected outlets and older houses often don't but should, GFI's have saved my worthless arse several times already.
              </em>
             </p>
             <p>
              <em>
               And now there are breakers that trip if there is a short in the wiring...since I have a lot of hidden romex in This Old House these are getting installed asap before I get around to replaceing the 60 year old romex with newer. Some cities are requiring them, they are 40-70$,)
              </em>
             </p>

            I love that you dont give a crap how it looks, but do care that it functions.
           </p>
           <p>
            I love how you used and re-purposed found objects, some that were "sought after" more than "found" but, you're more concerned, again, with the function.
           </p>
           <p>
            I totally love this attitude, it made me laugh:
            <br/>
           </p>
           <blockquote>
            <strong>
             I'm sure that an engineer could come up with a formula
            </strong>
            using the pump volume output numbers to find the exact size and number of holes to drill
            <strong>
             but my way works too.
            </strong>
           </blockquote>
           Some genius kossacks ought to start a new DK DIY Group and call it "Winging It". Heh.
           <p>
            But the best best part was seeing all the different birds just loving it. Wow.
           </p>

            Thank you.

        <li id="c80">
         <div class="cx" id="cx47079812">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Lovely, thx. My home-made bird bath is yard-sale
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47079812#c80?mode=alone;showrate=1#c80">
             5+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:278494">
              burnt out
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:34327">
              Damnit Janet
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163899">
              Polly Syllabic
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:70454">
              KenBee
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:31022">
              sockpuppet
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            iron pot holder with yard-sale plastic (but handsome) pot. I bought a cheap fountain pump, put big pot in iron potholder. Used knife to make a hole near the top of the pot. Ran fountain pump cord through that hole to outdoors extension cord.
           </p>
           <p>
            Fitted yard-sale plastic saucer (with holes punched) in top of pot. Sprinkled nice-looking rocks in saucer &amp; clean about every 3 weeks. The birds love it.
           </p>
          </div>

           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             I hope that's low voltage outdoor wiring.
            </p>
            <p>
             If not and it's 110v house power, it's gotta..GOTTA be on a GFI protected circuit, and the outdoor wires in conduit or buried as it used to show in the UBCode...better yet a stand alone solar powered pump for safety.
            </p>
            <p>
             <em>
              What runs my backlot pump?
             </em>
            </p>
            <p>
             <em>
              an extension cord snaked idioticly thru loose piled stuff overhead...but the ends are out of the sun and rain and moisture,and the business end is plugged into a GFI...
             </em>
             which is a device that trips should there be a path from the electricity to the ground, such as thru your wet hands or feet, it trips so fast you don't feel the short. And they work...until they don't,which is why the wiring should be as good as you can make it as well, or replace the setup with a solar powered pump.
            </p>
            <p>
             So many of us wing it and think cause we're clever we can get away with it for a while..it's all fun and games until someone gets fried. Done that too. Big surprise.
            </p>
           </div>
           <div class="cf">

        <li id="c115">
         <div class="cx" id="cx47083633">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Wow, beautiful!
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47083633#c115?mode=alone;showrate=1#c115">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:278494">
              burnt out
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163899">

             </a>
            </dd>

          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            That is a terrific idea!  I love seeing the birds at your bath.  Gorgeous photos.
           </p>
           <p>
            Our birdbath is in the shade under a thick canopy of trees. So it's staying pretty cool, although we're headed for double-digit temps this week, so I'll see if it stays cool. I just hadn't thought of it, that the water might get too hot.
           </p>
           <p>
            We also have a circulating fountain that seems to work pretty much like what you've designed there. The birds seem to really enjoy drinking from it and bathing in it. I saw a golden finch splashing in it today.
           </p>
           <p>
            I've seen mourning doves, crows, a stellar jay (today), two California towhees, and a fat male robin bathe in our birdbath.  I keep it a bit deep, so the little birds (like the goldfinches) only come to drink from it.  But the bigger birds just revel in it.
           </p>
           <p>
            I've been wanting another fountain for the garden. I like your design.  Thanks for sharing that!
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">

             Correction:
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1102903/47083696#c120?mode=alone;showrate=1#c120">
              2+ / 0-

            <p>
             We're headed for
             <strong>
              triple
             </strong>
             -digit temps this next week. eek.
            </p>
            <p>
             We Northern Californians have been pretty spoiled all summer, so far, with our cool 65-85 mild temps while the rest of the country has been boiling hot. Now it's our turn, apparently.  It's been a bit cooler here by the Bay, but the temps are gonna climb more every day until sometime next week ('til the end of the month, I heard one forecaster say).
            </p>
            <p>
             Thanks again, burnt out, for reminding us of doable and useful ways of helping out bird-people and other critter-folk in this hot weather.  Very thoughtful of you. :)

        <li id="c121">
         <div class="cx" id="cx47083726">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Add another saucer
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47083726#c121?mode=alone;showrate=1#c121">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:278494">
              burnt out
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163899">
              Polly Syllabic
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            Burnt Out: You can get the top bath you want by just adding another drilled-out saucer to the top, right side up.
            <br/>
            The water will run down the side of the top saucer, then down the side of the upside down saucer into the lower bath like it does now.
            <br/>
            And yes, I will be making something like this soon due to your inspiration. Thanks from 105 degree central Texas.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
           </p>

        <li id="c122">
         <div class="cx" id="cx47083916">
          <h5>
           <a class="de">
           </a>
           <span class="cu">
            Thanks for the project inspiration.
           </span>
           <span class="crd ntb">
            (
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47083916#c122?mode=alone;showrate=1#c122">
             2+ / 0-
            </a>
            )
           </span>
          </h5>
          <div class="crs">
           <dl>
            <dt>
             Recommended by:
            </dt>
            <dd>
             <a href="/user/uid:278494">
              burnt out
             </a>
             ,
             <a href="/user/uid:163899">
              Polly Syllabic
             </a>
            </dd>
           </dl>
          </div>
          <div class="ct">
           <p>
            I don't currently have flowing water in my bird baths but I do have one in the sun and one in the shade. Some birds prefer the open sunny location. Others like the cover by the shady one. Have to fill the sunny one every day. Also flush the shady one while I'm at it, but it would last for several days before drying up. Seems like bird dander would be a problem for the pump filter.
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="cf">
           <p class="sig">
            Dot farmer
           </p>
           <p class="cb">
            by
            <a href="/user/uid:174047">
             dot farmer
            </a>
            on
            <a href="/comments/1102903/47083916#c122">
             Thu Aug 09, 2012 at 03:59:44 AM PDT
            </a>
           </p>
           <p class="cl">
           </p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </li>
        <ul class="cm i1" id="k47083916">
         <li id="c126">
          <div class="cx" id="cx47083993">
           <h5>
            <a class="de">
            </a>
            <span class="cu">
             You're welcome dot farmer. Most of what I see in
            </span>
            <span class="crd ntb">
             (
             <a href="/comments/1102903/47083993#c126?mode=alone;showrate=1#c126">
              2+ / 0-
             </a>
             )
            </span>
           </h5>
           <div class="crs">
            <dl>
             <dt>
              Recommended by:
             </dt>
             <dd>
              <a href="/user/uid:163899">
               Polly Syllabic
              </a>
              ,
              <a href="/user/uid:174047">
               dot farmer
              </a>
             </dd>
            </dl>
           </div>
           <div class="ct">
            <p>
             the filter when I clean it are bits and pieces of sunflower seeds and small bits of grass and such. I plan to wrap the drain pipe with screen wire and that should keep most of that stuff from every reaching the pump.
            </p>

		  } else {
		    var subdomain = document.location.hostname.split('.')[0];
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Vertical', { name: subdomain });
		  }
		}
		
		if ($('.ratinate').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.ratinate').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Comment') });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-addRating.type-story').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-addRating.type-story').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Recommended Story') });
		}
		
		if ($("form[action$='publishHow']").length &gt; 0) {
		  $(document).ready(function() {
			  $('.type-story.do-publishHow').click(function() { DailyKos.Metrics.track('Published Story') });
			 });
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/user/) &amp;&amp; $('li.here').length &gt; 0) {
		  if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Stream/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Stream', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:first li.here').children('a').html().match(/Profile/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Profile', { name: $('.name').children('a').html() });
		  } else if ($('.pageMenu:last li.here').children('a').html().match(/My Recent Replies/)) {
		    DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Replies');
		  }
		} 
		
		if ($('#search-tabbed').length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Searched');
		}
		
		if ($('#group-tables').length &gt; 0) {
			DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Groups List');
		}
		
		if (document.location.pathname.match(/^\/groups/) &amp;&amp; $("#group_info").length &gt; 0) {
		  DailyKos.Metrics.track('Viewed Group', { name: $('.name').children('a').text() });
		}
		
		if ($('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').length &gt; 0) {
		  $('.do-hotlist.type-user, .do-unHotlist.type-user').click(function() {
		    var nickName;
		    nickName = ($(this).prev('a').html() || $('.name a').html())
		    if ($(this).hasClass('do-hotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Followed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    } else if ($(this).hasClass('do-unHotlist')) {
		      DailyKos.Metrics.track('Unfollowed User', { nickname: nickName }) 
		    }    
		  });
		}
	}
  </script>
  <!-- end mixpanel -->
 </body>
</html>
